	</div>
</div>

							</nav>
						</div>
					</div>
				</div>

<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">US record label</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066479718">.mw-parser-output .infobox-subbox{padding:0;border:none;margin:-3px;width:auto;min-width:100%;font-size:100%;clear:none;float:none;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .infobox-3cols-child{margin:auto}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-header,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-subheader,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-above,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-title,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-image,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-full-data,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-below{text-align:center}</style><table class="infobox vcard"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-above fn org" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1129693374"><div class="hlist"><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">Hip hop</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Country of origin</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Location</th><td class="infobox-data label"><a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Official website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://hstlgng32.com">hstlgng32<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Grand Hustle Records</b> (formerly <b>Grand Hustle Entertainment</b>), also known as <b>Hustle Gang Music</b>, is an <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>–based hip hop <a href="/wiki/Record_label" title="Record label">record label</a>, founded in 2003, by American rapper <a href="/wiki/T.I." title="T.I.">T.I.</a> and his manager Jason Geter.<sup id="cite_ref-xxlmagxxl_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxlmagxxl-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-apple1_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apple1-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The label was distributed by <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Records" title="Atlantic Records">Atlantic Records</a> until December 2012. It currently operates as an <a href="/wiki/Independent_record_label" title="Independent record label">independent record label</a>. Its roster has included the artists <a href="/wiki/8Ball_%26_MJG" title="8Ball &amp; MJG">8Ball &amp; MJG</a>, <a href="/wiki/B.o.B" title="B.o.B">B.o.B</a>, <a href="/wiki/Killer_Mike" title="Killer Mike">Killer Mike</a>, <a href="/wiki/Young_Dro" title="Young Dro">Young Dro</a>, <a href="/wiki/DJ_Drama" title="DJ Drama">DJ Drama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meek_Mill" title="Meek Mill">Meek Mill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chip_(rapper)" title="Chip (rapper)">Chip</a>, <a href="/wiki/Travis_Scott" title="Travis Scott">Travis Scott</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Trae_tha_Truth" title="Trae tha Truth">Trae tha Truth</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>  the latter of whom also serves as the label's vice president. The label also houses a roster of <a href="/wiki/Record_producer" title="Record producer">record producers</a>, which has included <a href="/wiki/Lil%27_C_(record_producer)" title="Lil&#39; C (record producer)">Lil' C</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mars_(record_producer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mars (record producer)">Mars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nard_%26_B" title="Nard &amp; B">Nard &amp; B</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The label has released 33 <a href="/wiki/Studio_album" class="mw-redirect" title="Studio album">studio albums</a>, with 14 of them <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">certified gold</a> or higher by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The label has released six albums that reached number one on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart, namely <i><a href="/wiki/King_(T.I._album)" title="King (T.I. album)">King</a></i> (2006), <i><a href="/wiki/T.I._vs._T.I.P." title="T.I. vs. T.I.P.">T.I. vs. T.I.P.</a></i> (2007), <i><a href="/wiki/Paper_Trail" title="Paper Trail">Paper Trail</a></i> (2008), <i><a href="/wiki/B.o.B_Presents:_The_Adventures_of_Bobby_Ray" title="B.o.B Presents: The Adventures of Bobby Ray">The Adventures of Bobby Ray</a></i> (2010), <i><a href="/wiki/Birds_in_the_Trap_Sing_McKnight" title="Birds in the Trap Sing McKnight">Birds in the Trap Sing McKnight</a></i> (2016) and <i><a href="/wiki/Astroworld_(album)" title="Astroworld (album)">Astroworld</a></i> (2018). Grand Hustle has released multiple <a href="/wiki/Top_40" title="Top 40">Top 40</a> <a href="/wiki/Hit_single" class="mw-redirect" title="Hit single">hit singles</a>, including "<a href="/wiki/Bring_Em_Out_(song)" title="Bring Em Out (song)">Bring 'Em Out</a>", "<a href="/wiki/What_You_Know_(T.I._song)" title="What You Know (T.I. song)">What You Know</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Shoulder_Lean" title="Shoulder Lean">Shoulder Lean</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Dead_and_Gone" title="Dead and Gone">Dead and Gone</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Airplanes_(song)" title="Airplanes (song)">Airplanes</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Magic_(B.o.B_song)" title="Magic (B.o.B song)">Magic</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Strange_Clouds_(song)" title="Strange Clouds (song)">Strange Clouds</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Both_of_Us" title="Both of Us">Both of Us</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Antidote_(Travis_Scott_song)" title="Antidote (Travis Scott song)">Antidote</a>" and more. Among those singles, six of them went on to reach the number one spot on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart – "<a href="/wiki/Whatever_You_Like" title="Whatever You Like">Whatever You Like</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Live_Your_Life_(T.I._song)" title="Live Your Life (T.I. song)">Live Your Life</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Nothin%27_on_You" title="Nothin&#39; on You">Nothin' on You</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Sicko_Mode" title="Sicko Mode">Sicko Mode</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Highest_in_the_Room" title="Highest in the Room">Highest in the Room</a>".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_Hustle_Records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="2003.E2.80.9311:_Beginnings_and_various_signings"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2003–11:_Beginnings_and_various_signings">2003–11: Beginnings and various signings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_Hustle_Records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 2003–11: Beginnings and various signings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Due to the poor commercial reception of his debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/I%27m_Serious" title="I&#39;m Serious">I'm Serious</a></i>, T.I. was released from his <a href="/wiki/Arista_Records" title="Arista Records">Arista Records</a> contract.<sup id="cite_ref-RouteBack_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RouteBack-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> He then formed Grand Hustle Entertainment and began releasing several <a href="/wiki/Mixtape" title="Mixtape">mixtapes</a>, with the assistance of <a href="/wiki/DJ_Drama" title="DJ Drama">DJ Drama</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RouteBack_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RouteBack-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> He resurfaced in the summer of 2003, alongside fellow Atlanta rapper and former label-mate <a href="/wiki/Bone_Crusher_(rapper)" title="Bone Crusher (rapper)">Bone Crusher</a>, on the song "<a href="/wiki/Never_Scared_(song)" title="Never Scared (song)">Never Scared</a>", and he signed a <a href="/wiki/Joint_venture" title="Joint venture">joint venture</a> deal with <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Records" title="Atlantic Records">Atlantic Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> T.I. released his second album <i><a href="/wiki/Trap_Muzik" title="Trap Muzik">Trap Muzik</a></i> on August 19, 2003, through Grand Hustle Records; it debuted at number four and sold 109,000 copies in its first week.<sup id="cite_ref-king_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-king-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> It spawned the singles "<a href="/wiki/24%27s" class="mw-redirect" title="24&#39;s">24s</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Be_Easy_(T.I._Song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Be Easy (T.I. Song)">Be Easy</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Rubberband_Man" class="mw-redirect" title="Rubberband Man">Rubberband Man</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Let%27s_Get_Away" title="Let&#39;s Get Away">Let's Get Away</a>". In March 2004, a <a href="/wiki/Warrant_(law)" title="Warrant (law)">warrant</a> was issued for T.I.'s arrest after he violated his <a href="/wiki/Probation" title="Probation">probation</a> of a 1997 drug conviction.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> He was sentenced to three years in <a href="/wiki/Prison" title="Prison">prison</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-three_years_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-three_years-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2005, fellow <a href="/wiki/Bankhead,_Atlanta" title="Bankhead, Atlanta">Bankhead</a>-based rapper Alfamega signed a deal with Grand Hustle Records. In July 2005, the label released the <a href="/wiki/Hustle_%26_Flow_(soundtrack)" title="Hustle &amp; Flow (soundtrack)">soundtrack to the film</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Hustle_%26_Flow" title="Hustle &amp; Flow">Hustle &amp; Flow</a></i>. The soundtrack included the song "<a href="/wiki/It%27s_Hard_out_Here_for_a_Pimp" title="It&#39;s Hard out Here for a Pimp">It's Hard out Here for a Pimp</a>", which won an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Academy Award for Best Original Song">Academy Award for Best Original Song</a>. Also in 2005, T.I. added American <a href="/wiki/Soul_(music)" class="mw-redirect" title="Soul (music)">soul</a> singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Governor_(singer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Governor (singer)">Governor</a> to the Grand Hustle roster, after Atlantic Records chose T.I. to act as his mentor. Atlantic Records' plan for Governor, who joined Atlantic's roster almost four years prior, was to market him a devotee, or a card-carrying member of T.I.'s "camp".<sup id="cite_ref-governor_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-governor-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Atlantic first tried to pair him with record producer <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>, and then with <a href="/wiki/Gangsta_rap" title="Gangsta rap">gangsta rapper</a> <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a>. Both plans fell through. In search of quick street credibility, the label brokered a deal for the singer to join T.I.'s imprint.<sup id="cite_ref-governor_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-governor-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> After appearing on several of DJ Drama's <i>Gangsta Grillz</i> mixtapes, Governor later released his Grand Hustle debut <i><a href="/wiki/Son_of_Pain" title="Son of Pain">Son of Pain</a></i>, in September 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-governor_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-governor-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By early 2006, T.I. had signed fellow <a href="/wiki/Bankhead_(Atlanta)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bankhead (Atlanta)">Bankhead</a>-based rapper <a href="/wiki/Young_Dro" title="Young Dro">Young Dro</a>, to the label. Young Dro released the single "<a href="/wiki/Shoulder_Lean" title="Shoulder Lean">Shoulder Lean</a>" in the summer of 2006. It had heavy rotation on <a href="/wiki/Black_Entertainment_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Entertainment Television">BET</a> and <a href="/wiki/MTV2" title="MTV2">MTV2</a>, and its cellular phone <a href="/wiki/Ringtone" title="Ringtone">ringtone</a> sold over 500,000 units. The single is featured on Dro's major-label debut <i><a href="/wiki/Best_Thang_Smokin%27" title="Best Thang Smokin&#39;">Best Thang Smokin'</a></i>, released in late August the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In December 2006, the label released <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Hustle_Presents:_In_da_Streetz_Volume_4" title="Grand Hustle Presents: In da Streetz Volume 4">Grand Hustle Presents: In da Streetz Volume 4</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Compilation_album" title="Compilation album">compilation album</a> featuring contributions from several Grand Hustle artists including aforementioned newcomers Alfamega, Young Dro and Governor. The compilation's title comes from a mixtape series entitled <i>In da Streetz</i>, that T.I. and his hip hop ensemble <a href="/wiki/P$C" class="mw-redirect" title="P$C">Pimp $quad Click</a> (P$C), released in their early careers.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On October 13, 2007, federal authorities arrested T.I. four hours before the <a href="/wiki/BET_Hip_Hop_Awards" title="BET Hip Hop Awards">BET Hip Hop Awards</a> in Atlanta.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> He was charged with two felonies&#160;– <a href="/wiki/National_Firearms_Act" title="National Firearms Act">possession of three unregistered machine guns and two silencers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gun_Control_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Gun Control Act">possession of firearms by a convicted felon</a>. The arrest was made in the parking lot of a downtown shopping center. T.I. was arrested after allegedly trying to purchase the guns from a "cooperating witness" with the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Alcohol,_Tobacco,_Firearms_and_Explosives" title="Bureau of Alcohol, Tobacco, Firearms and Explosives">Bureau of Alcohol, Tobacco, Firearms and Explosives</a>. According to federal officials, the witness had been cooperating with authorities a few days prior to the T.I. arrest. The witness had been working as T.I.'s bodyguard since July, authorities said.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2008, T.I. signed up-and-coming Atlanta-based musician <a href="/wiki/B.o.B" title="B.o.B">B.o.B</a>, who signed a joint partnership deal with Grand Hustle and super producer <a href="/wiki/Jim_Jonsin" title="Jim Jonsin">Jim Jonsin</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Rebel_Rock_Entertainment" class="mw-redirect" title="Rebel Rock Entertainment">Rebel Rock Entertainment</a>, under Atlantic Records. B.o.B was later featured on T.I.'s album <i><a href="/wiki/Paper_Trail" title="Paper Trail">Paper Trail</a></i> (2008) on the track "On Top of the World", which also featured <a href="/wiki/Ludacris" title="Ludacris">Ludacris</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> In June 2008, T.I. announced the signing of <a href="/wiki/Southern_hip_hop" title="Southern hip hop">Southern hip hop</a> duo <a href="/wiki/8Ball_%26_MJG" title="8Ball &amp; MJG">8Ball &amp; MJG</a> to Grand Hustle, during his <i><a href="/wiki/WHTA" title="WHTA">Hot 107-9</a> Birthday Bash</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-8ballmjg_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8ballmjg-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In December 2008, <a href="/wiki/Killer_Mike" title="Killer Mike">Killer Mike</a>, whom T.I. previously collaborated with on the 2003 hit single "<a href="/wiki/Never_Scared_(song)" title="Never Scared (song)">Never Scared</a>", confirmed he signed a recording contract with Grand Hustle.<sup id="cite_ref-killermike_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-killermike-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2008, T.I. also signed <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>-based rapper <a href="/wiki/Meek_Mill" title="Meek Mill">Meek Mill</a> to Grand Hustle. Shortly after, Mill was arrested, charged with a crime and ordered to serve seven months in jail. Mill was released during the early portion of 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Due to T.I.'s and Mill's respective legal troubles, Mill was never able to release an album under Grand Hustle and they parted ways in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-grandhustle_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grandhustle-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2008, P$C member <a href="/wiki/AK_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="AK (rapper)">AK</a>, also known as AK the Razorman, began to express his discontent with the label and his longtime friend T.I.:<sup id="cite_ref-ak_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ak-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In a 2011 interview with Inday, a Grand Hustle marketing promoter, he confirmed AK and <a href="/wiki/Yung_L.A." title="Yung L.A.">Yung L.A.</a> were no longer a part of the label.<sup id="cite_ref-ak1_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ak1-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In May 2009, T.I. dropped rapper Alfamega, who signed in 2005, after reports surfaced of his past as a <a href="/wiki/Drug_Enforcement_Administration" title="Drug Enforcement Administration">DEA</a> <a href="/wiki/Informant" title="Informant">informant</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> A short-lived feud between the two later embroiled, with Alfamega releasing a <a href="/wiki/Diss_track" class="mw-redirect" title="Diss track">diss track</a> titled "Greenlight", in March 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 1, 2010, T.I. and his wife <a href="/wiki/Tameka_Cottle" title="Tameka Cottle">Tameka "Tiny" Cottle</a>, were arrested on drug charges in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The arrest for drug charges led to T.I. being sentenced on October 15, 2010 to 11 months in prison for violating the terms of his probation, specifically for possessing ecstasy, testing positive for opiates and associating with a convicted felon, namely his <a href="/wiki/P$C" class="mw-redirect" title="P$C">P$C</a> cohort <a href="/wiki/C-Rod" title="C-Rod">C-Rod</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> However, on October 25, the drug charges against T.I. were dropped.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> On November 1, T.I. reported back to the Forrest City Federal Facility to serve his 11-month sentence.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> His date of release was set to be September 29, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-bop_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bop-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> His seventh album <i><a href="/wiki/No_Mercy_(T.I._album)" title="No Mercy (T.I. album)">No Mercy</a></i>, was released on December 7, 2010, during his imprisonment. The album peaked at number four in the US and it sold over 159,000 copies in its first week.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> RIAA certified <i>No Mercy</i> Gold, with over 500,000 copies sold.
</p>
<h3><span id="2011.E2.80.932016:_Get_Dough_or_Die_series"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2011–2016:_Get_Dough_or_Die_series">2011–2016: <i>Get Dough or Die</i> series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_Hustle_Records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2011–2016: Get Dough or Die series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2011, T.I. signed his youngest brother Bryce Harris, better known by his stage name GFM Bryyce.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> In late 2011, Grand Hustle solo artists Shad da God, Spodee and Yung Booke, came together to form the hip hop group D.O.P.E. (an acronym for Destroying Other People's Egos). D.O.P.E.'s first notable song, titled "Harry Potter" and produced by <a href="/wiki/Hit-Boy" title="Hit-Boy">Hit-Boy</a>, was included on T.I.'s fifth solo mixtape, <i>Fuck da City Up</i>, which was released January 1, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> On March 1, 2012, T.I. revealed he signed <a href="/wiki/Rapper" class="mw-redirect" title="Rapper">rappers</a> <a href="/wiki/Iggy_Azalea" title="Iggy Azalea">Iggy Azalea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chip_(rapper)" title="Chip (rapper)">Chip</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trae_tha_Truth" title="Trae tha Truth">Trae tha Truth</a>, to Grand Hustle Records.<sup id="cite_ref-Rap-Up_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rap-Up-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3LittleDigs_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3LittleDigs-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> T.I. was <a href="/wiki/Executive_producer" title="Executive producer">executive producer</a> on Azalea's debut <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">EP</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Glory_(EP)" title="Glory (EP)">Glory</a></i> and was featured on the lead single "Murda Bizness", which premiered March 26, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The EP was released on July 30, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> On October 9, 2012, T.I., Iggy Azalea, <a href="/wiki/B.o.B" title="B.o.B">B.o.B</a>, Chip and Trae tha Truth, were all featured on the annual <a href="/wiki/BET_Hip_Hop_Awards" title="BET Hip Hop Awards">BET Hip Hop Awards</a> cypher.<sup id="cite_ref-cypher_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cypher-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, Chip, formerly known as Chipmunk, also released his first project with Grand Hustle, a mixtape entitled <i><a href="/wiki/London_Boy_(mixtape)" title="London Boy (mixtape)">London Boy</a></i>. The mixtape, which features several appearances from Grand Hustle artists, including Iggy Azalea and T.I on the <a href="/wiki/Posse_cut" title="Posse cut">posse cut</a> "Hustle Gang", was released on December 25, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> In early January 2013, B.o.B announced an upcoming Grand Hustle compilation album titled <i>Hustle Gang</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-xxlmag_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxlmag-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On January 18, 2013, it was announced T.I. drew a close to his 10-year contract with Atlantic Records the month before, after releasing <i><a href="/wiki/Trouble_Man:_Heavy_Is_the_Head" title="Trouble Man: Heavy Is the Head">Trouble Man: Heavy Is the Head</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-xxl_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxl-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> It was reported he proposed a $75 million deal for any label that wanted to provide a home for him and his imprint. <a href="/wiki/TMZ_(website)" class="mw-redirect" title="TMZ (website)">TMZ</a> reported that T.I. had drawn up the details, which included exclusive signing of all Grand Hustle artists.<sup id="cite_ref-xxl_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxl-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> T.I. allegedly negotiated with several big names in the industry: there were reports that <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> was looking to sign T.I., hoping to add him to the <a href="/wiki/Roc_Nation" title="Roc Nation">Roc Nation</a> roster; T.I. had dinner with <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>, who is thought to have proposed an <a href="/wiki/Interscope" class="mw-redirect" title="Interscope">Interscope</a> signing to the rapper; <a href="/wiki/Sony_Music_Entertainment" class="mw-redirect" title="Sony Music Entertainment">Sony</a> reportedly offered T.I. $50 Million, and spoke with Universal later that week.<sup id="cite_ref-xxl_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxl-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2013, T.I. and <a href="/wiki/B.o.B" title="B.o.B">B.o.B</a> filmed the music video for "<a href="/wiki/Memories_Back_Then" title="Memories Back Then">Memories Back Then</a>", a song featuring <a href="/wiki/Kendrick_Lamar" title="Kendrick Lamar">Kendrick Lamar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kris_Stephens" title="Kris Stephens">Kris Stephens</a>. The song, which was recorded for <i>Trouble Man: Heavy Is the Head</i>, failed to appear on <i>Trouble Man</i> due to sample-clearance issues, it was announced to be being released as the lead single from the upcoming <i>Grand Hustle Presents: Hustle Gang</i> compilation album.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The music video for "Memories Back Then", directed by Philly Fly Boy, was released April 22, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The song was then officially released via iTunes the next day.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The song has since debuted at #88 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>.
</p><p>On April 4, T.I. revealed the label would release a mixtape titled, <i><a href="/wiki/G.D.O.D._(Get_Dough_or_Die)" title="G.D.O.D. (Get Dough or Die)">G.D.O.D. (Get Dough or Die)</a></i>, during the first week of May 2013, preceding the compilation album.<sup id="cite_ref-GDOD_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GDOD-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> On April 19, 2013, T.I. formally introduced <a href="/wiki/GOOD_Music" title="GOOD Music">GOOD Music</a> producer <a href="/wiki/Travis_Scott" title="Travis Scott">Travis Scott</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> winning songwriter Kris Stephens, as Grand Hustle signees.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> On April 28, a release date for the mixtape would later be announced to be May 7, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> As promised the mixtape was released on May 7, featuring 20 tracks and contributions from Grand Hustle artists T.I., <a href="/wiki/Mitchelle%27l" title="Mitchelle&#39;l">Mitchelle'l</a>, B.o.B, Young Dro, Big Kuntry King, Trae tha Truth, D.O.P.E., <a href="/wiki/Travis_Scott" title="Travis Scott">Travis Scott</a>, Chip, Kris Stephens, Mac Boney, Doe B and Shad da God (formerly Rich Kid Shawty).<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> "Problems", "Poppin' 4 Sum",<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> "Kemosabe",<sup id="cite_ref-iTunes_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iTunes-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> and "Here I Go" were released as singles from the mixtape over the following months.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> In a May 8, 2013 interview, T.I. said that he was in talks of possibly signing American recording artists <a href="/wiki/Yo_Gotti" title="Yo Gotti">Yo Gotti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Problem_(rapper)" title="Problem (rapper)">Problem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeremih" title="Jeremih">Jeremih</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kirko_Bangz" title="Kirko Bangz">Kirko Bangz</a> to Grand Hustle.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On December 28, 2013, Glenn Thomas, better known by his stage name Doe B, died after being shot in his home state of <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">Alabama</a> with Mike Feez. His manager DJ Frank White confirmed Doe B's death via Twitter.<sup id="cite_ref-thesource.com_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thesource.com-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> In February 2014, Grand Hustle collaborated with <a href="/wiki/DJ_Whoo_Kid" title="DJ Whoo Kid">DJ Whoo Kid</a>, <a href="/wiki/DJ_Skee" title="DJ Skee">DJ Skee</a> and DJ MLK, to release the compilation mixtape <i>SXEW Vol. 1: The Grand Hustle</i>, the trio's annual <a href="/wiki/SXSW" class="mw-redirect" title="SXSW">SXSW</a> inspired mixtape.<sup id="cite_ref-sxew_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sxew-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sxew2_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sxew2-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sxew3_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sxew3-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> The mixtape features appearances from T.I., Young Dro, Trae Tha Truth, Iggy Azalea and Doe B, the latter of which is featured on a song with T.I. and American rapper <a href="/wiki/Raekwon" title="Raekwon">Raekwon</a>, titled "I Wanna Know".<sup id="cite_ref-sxew_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sxew-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sxew2_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sxew2-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sxew3_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sxew3-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In an August 2014 interview with <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a>, T.I. revealed plans to release the Grand Hustle compilation, which is tentatively due in December, following <i><a href="/wiki/Paperwork_(T.I._album)" title="Paperwork (T.I. album)">Paperwork</a></i>: "What's holding up the <i>Hustle Gang</i> project is that we have some new additions to the mix, and we didn't wanna put out the project out without including or allowing those new additions to be part of it. Maybe we'll do a stroke of midnight release on New Years. We did that with <i>F**k Da City Up</i> and it did well, so maybe we'll try that again."<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> On September 19, 2014, the label released the second installment to the <i>G.D.O.D. (Get Dough or Die)</i> series.<sup id="cite_ref-gdod2_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gdod2-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Aside from Grand Hustle recording artists, the mixtape features additional appearances from Iggy Azalea, Meek Mill, <a href="/wiki/Young_Thug" title="Young Thug">Young Thug</a>, <a href="/wiki/Troy_Ave" title="Troy Ave">Troy Ave</a>, <a href="/wiki/Watch_The_Duck" class="mw-redirect" title="Watch The Duck">Watch The Duck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yo_Gotti" title="Yo Gotti">Yo Gotti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trey_Songz" title="Trey Songz">Trey Songz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rich_Homie_Quan" title="Rich Homie Quan">Rich Homie Quan</a>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-gdod2_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gdod2-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2015, it was announced the <a href="/wiki/OMG_(musical_group)" class="mw-redirect" title="OMG (musical group)">OMG Girlz</a>, the musical trio that included T.I.'s stepdaughter, was officially disestablished.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> In August 2015, D.O.P.E. member Spodee, announced he was no longer under Grand Hustle; during an interview he stated "Everybody know I was a loyal guy with Grand Hustle and Tip. And, you know, it's no bad blood. I'm not mad at Tip or anything like that, but I have the potential to be bigger than Tip or if not, just as big. So it was time, man. I outgrew that. [I was with Grand Hustle] for too long. Six years."<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> In response, T.I. commented "As we all go about our business and pleasure on this fine day today, allow me to remind you of two former young hopeful Grand Hustlers, who thought going against the glory and good graces of [the family] might be more beneficial to their campaign", referring to Yung L.A. and DG Yola.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2015, <a href="/wiki/Travis_Scott" title="Travis Scott">Travis Scott</a> released his debut studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Rodeo_(Travis_Scott_album)" title="Rodeo (Travis Scott album)">Rodeo</a></i>, under Grand Hustle and <a href="/wiki/Epic_Records" title="Epic Records">Epic Records</a>. The album was supported by two singles, "<a href="/wiki/3500_(song)" class="mw-redirect" title="3500 (song)">3500</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Antidote_(Travis_Scott_song)" title="Antidote (Travis Scott song)">Antidote</a>", the latter of which reached number 16 on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart and was certified platinum by the RIAA for sales over 1,000,000 digital downloads. In July 2016, Grand Hustle released a song under the namesake Hustle Gang, titled "40 Acres", featuring T.I. alongside fellow Atlanta-based rappers RaRa and Rossi.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 19, 2016, Grand Hustle released the compilation <i>H.G.O.E. (Hustle Gang Over Errrrythang)</i>, featuring guest appearances from Young Thug, <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Hart" title="Kevin Hart">Chocolate Droppa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Future_(rapper)" title="Future (rapper)">Future</a>, <a href="/wiki/Migos" title="Migos">Migos</a>, B.o.B, London Jae, Young Dro, Trae tha Truth, Lotto Savage, Shad da God, Kap G and more.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2017.E2.80.93present:_We_Want_Smoke"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2017–present:_We_Want_Smoke">2017–present: <i>We Want Smoke</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_Hustle_Records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2017–present: We Want Smoke">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In April 2017, American rappers Tokyo Jetz, RaRa, Translee and London Jae, were all revealed to be new members of the Grand Hustle roster.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 15, 2017, T.I. announced the Hustle Gang <a href="/wiki/Concert_tour" title="Concert tour">concert tour</a>. The Grand Hustle tour began on April 26 in Mobile, Alabama, going through 36 shows across the country before they wrapped up on June 11 in Jacksonville, Florida.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> In late March, Hustle Gang hosted an after-hours brunch and vibe event, at <a href="/wiki/South_by_Southwest" title="South by Southwest">South by Southwest</a> (SXSW), titled the Hustle Gang Experience, to feature the new Hustle Gang roster. T.I.'s son, Domani Harris, performed music from his recently released project <i>Constellation</i>, followed by RaRa with songs such as "FWM" off his debut project <i>I Am What I Am</i>. Tokyo Jetz went on to perform her <a href="/wiki/Viral_video" title="Viral video">viral</a> hit "DM", Yung Booke and London Jae performed "H.I.T.V.", and Trae Tha Truth performed records like "Swangin" and new music from T.I.'s forthcoming album.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 28, 2017, a song titled "Game 7" was released as the first single from Grand Hustle's compilation album <i>We Want Smoke</i>. The song features verses from T.I., RaRa and Rossi.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> The album's second single "Do No Wrong", was released in July and features verses from GFMBRYYCE, Young Dro and T.I.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> The album's third single "Friends", was released with an accompanying music video, on September 8.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> "Friends" features Hustle Gang rappers T.I., RaRa, Brandon Rossi, Tokyo Jetz, Trae tha Truth and Young Dro.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In an October 2017 interview with <a href="/wiki/HipHopDX" title="HipHopDX">HipHopDX</a>, when asked about Grand Hustle Records' upcoming albums, T.I. answered with: "<i><a href="/wiki/We_Want_Smoke" title="We Want Smoke">We Want Smoke</a></i> is out, and then Translee is coming out on November 27th, and Booke is October 27th, and you can wait until December 18th for mine. Just know that whenever you see The Chief [logo] on the project, it's gonna be absolute pandemonium. It gonna go hamburger."<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Publishing_deals">Publishing deals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_Hustle_Records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Publishing deals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Throughout the years, Grand Hustle Records has signed multiple artists (often in their respective early careers) to publishing deals. The following list documents notable artists who had signed such a contract at one point or another.
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Iggy_Azalea" title="Iggy Azalea">Iggy Azalea</a><sup id="cite_ref-hiphopdxazalea_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdxazalea-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kris_Stephens" title="Kris Stephens">Kris Stephens</a><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Spot_(rapper)" title="Spot (rapper)">Spot</a><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Zuse<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Branches">Branches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_Hustle_Records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Branches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><span class="anchor" id="Hustle_Gang"></span>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hustle_Gang">Hustle Gang</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_Hustle_Records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Hustle Gang">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1126788409">.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul{line-height:inherit;list-style:none;margin:0;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol li,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul li{margin-bottom:0}</style><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718"><table class="infobox vcard plainlist"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-above" style="background-color: #b0c4de; font-size: 125%;"><div class="">Hustle Gang</div></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><span class="nowrap">Years active</span></th><td class="infobox-data">2013–present</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Labels</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Roc_Nation" title="Roc Nation">Roc Nation</a>, Defiant, Grand Hustle</td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #b0c4de"></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Members</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/B.o.B" title="B.o.B">B.o.B</a><br />RaRa<br />Shad da God<br />Spodee<br /><a href="/wiki/T.I." title="T.I.">T.I.</a><br />Tokyo Jetz<br /><a href="/wiki/Trae_tha_Truth" title="Trae tha Truth">Trae tha Truth</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Young_Dro" title="Young Dro">Young Dro</a><br />Yung Booke</td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #b0c4de"></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><span class="nowrap">Past members</span></th><td class="infobox-data">Iggy Azalea, <a href="/wiki/Doe_B" title="Doe B">Doe B</a> (deceased)</td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #b0c4de"></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.hstlgng32.com/">www<wbr />.hstlgng32<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Hustle Gang</b> is an American <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_collective" class="mw-redirect" title="Hip hop collective">hip hop collective</a> composed of signees of Grand Hustle, introduced in 2013. The group's debut LP, <i><a href="/wiki/G.D.O.D._(Get_Dough_or_Die)" title="G.D.O.D. (Get Dough or Die)">GDOD: Get Dough or Die</a></i> was released the same year and co-released by record label Be Music. The group's 2017 releases were distributed by <a href="/wiki/Roc_Nation" title="Roc Nation">Roc Nation</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Smash_Factory">Smash Factory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_Hustle_Records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Smash Factory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><span class="anchor" id="Smash_Factory"></span>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1126788409"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718"><table class="infobox vcard plainlist"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-above" style="background-color: #b0c4de; font-size: 125%;"><div class="">Smash Factory</div></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><span class="nowrap">Years active</span></th><td class="infobox-data">2009–present</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Labels</th><td class="infobox-data">Grand Hustle</td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #b0c4de"></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Members</th><td class="infobox-data">T.I.<br /><a href="/wiki/1500_or_Nothin%27" title="1500 or Nothin&#39;">Lamar "Mars" Edwards</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Lil%27_C_(record_producer)" title="Lil&#39; C (record producer)">C Gutta</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Smash Factory was a production team composed of <a href="/wiki/T.I." title="T.I.">T.I.</a>, and Grand Hustle in-house producers, <a href="/wiki/1500_or_Nothin%27" title="1500 or Nothin&#39;">Lamar Edwards</a> (known as Mars or MyGuyMars) and <a href="/wiki/Lil%27_C_(record_producer)" title="Lil&#39; C (record producer)">C Gutta</a> (also known as Lil' C). The group has produced for the likes of <a href="/wiki/Nelly" title="Nelly">Nelly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Young_Dro" title="Young Dro">Young Dro</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="VisionMob">VisionMob</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_Hustle_Records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: VisionMob">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>VisionMob is a banner under Grand Hustle in which T.I. directs and or produces <a href="/wiki/Music_video" title="Music video">music videos</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In-house_producers">In-house producers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_Hustle_Records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: In-house producers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Grand Hustle Records also house a production wing, which serves as a group of in-house producers for the label.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current">Current</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_Hustle_Records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Current">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/DJ_Toomp" title="DJ Toomp">Aldrin "DJ Toomp" Davis</a> – known for producing T.I.'s <a href="/wiki/Hit_single" class="mw-redirect" title="Hit single">hit singles</a> "<a href="/wiki/24%27s" class="mw-redirect" title="24&#39;s">24's</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Be_Easy_(T.I._song)" title="Be Easy (T.I. song)">Be Easy</a>", "<a href="/wiki/U_Don%27t_Know_Me_(T.I._song)" title="U Don&#39;t Know Me (T.I. song)">U Don't Know Me</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/What_You_Know_(T.I._song)" title="What You Know (T.I. song)">What You Know</a>".</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lil%27_C_(record_producer)" title="Lil&#39; C (record producer)">Cordale "Lil' C" Quinn</a> – known for producing Young Dro's "<a href="/wiki/Shoulder_Lean" title="Shoulder Lean">Shoulder Lean</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Rubberband_Banks" title="Rubberband Banks">Rubberband Banks</a>", <a href="/wiki/Young_Jeezy" class="mw-redirect" title="Young Jeezy">Young Jeezy</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/My_Hood" title="My Hood">My Hood</a>" and T.I.'s "<a href="/wiki/Wit_Me" class="mw-redirect" title="Wit Me">Wit Me</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-MySpace_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MySpace-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>DJ MLK – Grand Hustle's resident <a href="/wiki/Disc_jockey" title="Disc jockey">disc jockey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Keith Mack – known for producing <a href="/wiki/Ludacris" title="Ludacris">Ludacris</a>' "<a href="/wiki/Act_a_Fool_(Ludacris_song)" title="Act a Fool (Ludacris song)">Act a Fool</a>" and several T.I. tracks, including the 2006 single "<a href="/wiki/Live_in_the_Sky" title="Live in the Sky">Live in the Sky</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Kevin "Khao" Cates – known for producing T.I.'s hit single "<a href="/wiki/Why_You_Wanna" title="Why You Wanna">Why You Wanna</a>", among other tracks for T.I. and other popular hip hop artists.<sup id="cite_ref-MySpace_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MySpace-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mars_(record_producer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mars (record producer)">Lamar "Mars" Edwards</a> – a member of production team <a href="/wiki/1500_or_Nothin%27" title="1500 or Nothin&#39;">1500 or Nothin'</a>, known for producing <a href="/wiki/Asher_Roth" title="Asher Roth">Asher Roth</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/G.R.I.N.D_(Get_Ready_It%27s_a_New_Day)" title="G.R.I.N.D (Get Ready It&#39;s a New Day)">G.R.I.N.D (Get Ready It's a New Day)</a>" and T.I.'s "<a href="/wiki/Love_This_Life" title="Love This Life">Love This Life</a>", among other songs from prominent artists.<sup id="cite_ref-smashfactory_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smashfactory-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Smash Factory – production team composed of T.I., Lil' C and Mars.<sup id="cite_ref-smashfactory_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smashfactory-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> They have produced songs such as "I Can't Help It" by T.I., "She's So Fly" by <a href="/wiki/Nelly" title="Nelly">Nelly</a> and "King on Set" by T.I., the latter of which was featured on the <a href="/wiki/More_than_a_Game_(soundtrack)" title="More than a Game (soundtrack)"><i>More than a Game</i> soundtrack</a>.</li>
<li>Two Band Geeks – production duo composed of Elliot Stroud and Billy Kang. Production credits include "I Know You Missed Me" by T.I., "Stand Up" by D.O.P.E. and more.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Elliot Stroud contributes solo production under the pseudonym 'Everybody Knows Stroud.'</li>
<li>TrackSlayerz – production duo composed of Dexter "INF" Randall and Demetri "Price" Duncan. Known for producing songs such as T.I.'s "<a href="/wiki/I%27m_Back_(song)" title="I&#39;m Back (song)">I'm Back</a>", <a href="/wiki/Jim_Jones_(rapper)" title="Jim Jones (rapper)">Jim Jones</a>' "Pulling Me Back" and <a href="/wiki/Yung_Joc" title="Yung Joc">Yung Joc</a>'s "Posted at da Store", among others.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Former">Former</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_Hustle_Records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Former">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>DJ Drama (2006–2011) – former resident disc jockey for the label</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nard_%26_B" title="Nard &amp; B">Nard &amp; B</a> (2007–2016)<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> – production duo composed of Bernard "Nard" Rosser and Brandon "B" Rackley. Known for producing several songs, including Yung L.A.'s "<a href="/wiki/Futuristic_Love_(Elroy)" title="Futuristic Love (Elroy)">Futuristic Love (Elroy)</a>", <a href="/wiki/Slim_Thug" title="Slim Thug">Slim Thug</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/So_High_(Slim_Thug_song)" title="So High (Slim Thug song)">So High</a>", and co-producing <a href="/wiki/Maino_(rapper)" title="Maino (rapper)">Maino</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/All_the_Above_(Maino_song)" title="All the Above (Maino song)">All the Above</a>", with high-profile producer <a href="/wiki/Just_Blaze" title="Just Blaze">Just Blaze</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MySpace_139-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MySpace-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personnel">Personnel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_Hustle_Records&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Personnel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li>Joe McLaren – artist development, engineer</li>

<li>Nikeya Gray – operations manager</li>
<li>Mark Jackson – executive VP of A&amp;R<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Vernell Woods – technology director<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li></ul>
